<div id="review_65735171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65735171" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2582987-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304572013p2/2582987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65735171?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/2582987-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65735171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3956820128443180622">If I could split this book in half and devide it into two stories (which is really what it is anyhow) one half would get 5 stars and the other half would get well... what you see above. Now, sense this book's main focus is on the bad half of the book, I'll have to give it the one lonely star you see floating above. <br/><br/>This is the finale of Crogan's Pellinor series. She has very impresive J.R.R. Tolkein like writing skills and incorperates more detail, history, and poetic naration into to her storie</span>
  <span id="freeText3956820128443180622" style="display:none">If I could split this book in half and devide it into two stories (which is really what it is anyhow) one half would get 5 stars and the other half would get well... what you see above. Now, sense this book's main focus is on the bad half of the book, I'll have to give it the one lonely star you see floating above. <br /><br />This is the finale of Crogan's Pellinor series. She has very impresive J.R.R. Tolkein like writing skills and incorperates more detail, history, and poetic naration into to her stories than many authors dare to today. I comend her for her efforts and I'm a big fan of her writing style but I aslo had big issues with our protagonist, Mearad, who had been likable up until this point. <br /><br />Mearad and Cadvan are making the final stretch in their journey to defeat the dark and stop the spreading disease of hate and distruction. Their little pilgrimage doesn't involve much excitement. They end up in the feilds of *blank*, waiting in a nearbye cave while Mearad goes through all these mental trials and eventually excepts all her evilness to gain complete control of her powers (or rather to let her powers take complete control of her)and defeat the evils residing within Pellinor. <br /><br />This is were my own sense of morality gets involved. <br /><br />It didn't really seem to me that Mearad was realizing her evils and compensating for them, and admitting to herself "Yeah, that was wrong." It super hard to explian but it really seemed like she was taking advantage of her evilness and using it for the betterment of man kind. This... I don't even know how to direct it. This bit of philospophy seemed all wrong and mixed up to me. Shouldn't you truly be embrasing your good side while admitting your wrong doings and puting them in the past. I look at it from a slightly religious point of veiw and it seems just... wrong. I had trouble believing in Mearad again, her quest, and her sense of perpous. <br /><br />Now, before I could really appreciate Mearad's plight. Months ago she was a slave unjustly forced into ignorance. She was the daughter of a great house and she'd blocked out the memories of the wrongdoings done toher so she could no longer be hurt by those actions. She was taken by cruelty and forced into and even crueler reality, a reality that was beautiful but was rapidly being consumed by darkness. And it was all up to her to save it. I fealt a deap pit widen in my stomach when she killed a bard back on before this book, but she payed dearly for it and she was able to admit her corruption but it didn't seem like she payed such a great price in the Singing. But then again, I don't even know if she was Mearad when she let both light and dark take over her very being. She was almost in a trance, a tool for the elements to take over. But it still didn't feel right. I don't like reading through a book and feeling guilty about it.<br /><br />Now, on a less philosophical and perhaps anthropological note. <br /><br />The rest of the story is brilliantly written except... the romance is a little bit less than satisfying. Frankly, I didn't see the Mearad/Cadvan conection until I read a few reviews and it was pointed out by readers. I didn't find it all that romantic from the start. But once it was there, it was there. It was odd for me scince Cadvan was so much older than her like... 80 years at the least. It was like Twilight except Cadvan looked about 30 years older while Mearad stayed... 16 if I remember corectly? Also, it was one of those deals that really ticks me off where the romance is realized on only the last couple pages. <br /><br />As for Soliman, that was awesome! I love that guy. He finds someone to be with and he has to fight for her while venturing into wastelands where he has so much to loose. He's a beautiful character and I miss him! I almost cried when I read the apendicies, finding out what happened to him. He's deffinately my favorite. <br /><br />As for Hem, poor lad, he still gets pushed around a bit as far as dialogue. Croggon has a tendency to insult the inteligence of her younger characters by crooning to them. Hem later proves him self as a passionate bard by... well, I can't tell you. Lets just say Soliman's life is on the line and Hem is perhaps the only one that could save him. <br /><br />The conclusion wasn't all that climatic and the book as a whole wasn't my favorite, though I would say Croggon is a very seccesful author. This was just a flop and hopefully the next time around she'll be able to show us what she's got. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3956820128443180622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2753040888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2753040888" />
    <a title="Sophia Barsuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84773901-sophia-barsuhn"><img alt="Sophia Barsuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557366016p2/84773901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2753040888?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia Barsuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia Barsuhn" href="/user/show/84773901-sophia-barsuhn">Sophia Barsuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2753040888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4198807300383374698">Well, it's done. After a year and a half, I've finished all five of the Pellinor books. It's been quite a journey. <br/><br/>The Bone Queen and The Naming were both very good, but I think after that the series went steadily downhill, and it hurts to say that, because I wanted to love these books. I know they're supposed to be a reimagining of The Lord of the Rings, and that's one of my favorite books ever, but these books aren't as good, especially The Singing. Let me try to organize my thoughts here.<br/><br/>Let'</span>
  <span id="freeText4198807300383374698" style="display:none">Well, it's done. After a year and a half, I've finished all five of the Pellinor books. It's been quite a journey. <br /><br />The Bone Queen and The Naming were both very good, but I think after that the series went steadily downhill, and it hurts to say that, because I wanted to love these books. I know they're supposed to be a reimagining of The Lord of the Rings, and that's one of my favorite books ever, but these books aren't as good, especially The Singing. Let me try to organize my thoughts here.<br /><br />Let's start with the characters. Except for a few moments here and there, they all feel flat and thin as paper. There's a scene in this book where Malgorn is obviously supposed to be like Théoden King defending Helm's Deep, but it doesn't ring true because he's barely been in these books and you don't actually know him. Same with Nelac. I feel like he's supposed to be like Gandalf, but he's hardly ever there, and when he is, he doesn't do anything. Hekibal especially is flat. I'm told again and again that she's brave and true and funny and beautiful, but I just didn't see it. <br /><br />Speaking of Hekibal, I feel like her relationship with Saliman came out of nowhere and didn't add too much to the story. I also like how the one conversation she has exclusively with Maerad (that we see) is about men. I hated how Hem and Saliman had absolutely no chemistry in this book, in sharp contrast to The Crow. And while I'm on the subject of relationships, let's talk about my least favorite one in this whole series: Maerad and Dernhil.<br /><br />I didn't understand the author's need to beat this dead horse into the ground. First of all, in The Naming, why didn't Dernhil just ASK if he could kiss Maerad? The whole part where she scratched him could have been avoided if he had just ASKED if he could kiss her. Then she spends the rest of The Naming, part of The Riddle, AND part of The Singing angsting over him and saying that she loved him. I'm sorry, but I don't care what excuse you use for insta-love. Here, it's, "Dernhil was well-versed in The Way of the Heart". NO. I'm not buying it. It just bothers me that Maerad feels guilty for her past trauma and blames everything on herself when it was Dernhil who kissed her and on top of that had the audacity to say he forgot himself because of her beauty. NO. Fuck off with that excuse. I can't stand it.<br /><br />The ending was anticlimactic. In LoTR, there's a huge battle and an incredibly moving scene of Frodo and Sam that always makes me cry. I feel like the ending of The Singing wanted to be like that, but it didn't hit the mark for me. Maybe because I simply didn't care about any of the characters by that point. I started out caring, and by the end of the series I was just tired. <br /><br />I would read an entire romance about Cadvan and Dernhil, or a whole book about Selmana (the best character in The Bone Queen). It kind of hurts me to give this book only two stars, because this is not a bad series. It just wasn't my cup of tea. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4198807300383374698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82390710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82390710" />
    <a title="Rah~ri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/564380-rah-ri"><img alt="Rah~ri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232771590p2/564380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82390710?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rah~ri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rah~ri" href="/user/show/564380-rah-ri">Rah~ri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82390710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6220755829385508288">Just read these? <br/><br/>Lifted my "new book ban" :) <br/><br/>Was going to wait till Next month <br/>but had hit a no sleep streak <br/>and went to the book store...? <br/>(Bad thing to do! So bad? love it though!) <br/><br/>Nothing intrigued me about these books <br/>... almost nothing? <br/>Never even heard of these books. <br/>Wasn't impressed by the covers <br/>(All books should be judged by there covers.). <br/>Didn't care about the story... sounded cutesy? young. <br/>But they were the thickest ones i could find! <br/>and there was a set of four!!! <br/><br/>Was mainly looki</span>
  <span id="freeText6220755829385508288" style="display:none">Just read these? <br /><br />Lifted my "new book ban" :) <br /><br />Was going to wait till Next month <br />but had hit a no sleep streak <br />and went to the book store...? <br />(Bad thing to do! So bad? love it though!) <br /><br />Nothing intrigued me about these books <br />... almost nothing? <br />Never even heard of these books. <br />Wasn't impressed by the covers <br />(All books should be judged by there covers.). <br />Didn't care about the story... sounded cutesy? young. <br />But they were the thickest ones i could find! <br />and there was a set of four!!! <br /><br />Was mainly looking for a book that would last more than a night. <br />... and i could limit my time,right?...only an hour or two a night??? <br />and figured i could maybe make these last for a week a book? <br />So i held the first of the series and some other thick book up <br />to a lady that was walking by and blatantly asked "Which one?" <br />She stopped looked at me and then picked this up <br />(she still thought i might be crazy but the curiosity of a book addict got her!) <br />She told me She liked the cover?!? LOL? <br />Ok! <br />This is the one! <br /><br />... got the first three... <br />Finished them to fast &amp; read the third one in an extreme slow panic, <br />Was trying not to finish it! <br />Was surprised how attached i became to the characters ! <br />Didn't want to finish it then get stuck in a snow storm <br />unable to get to a book store for weeks and weeks?!? <br />it would be sad? Wouldn't it? <br /><br />They were cutesy, lol? <br />and young. <br />and am not sure of the poetry??? <br />Something was lost in translation ;) <br />But also engaging. <br />Adventure, songs, magic, war, and hidden Love... <br />Found myself driving and thinking about the story <br />and the directions their "lives" might take??? <br />It's one of the few books that i can say <br />i appreciate the ending. <br />Books so often like to just end. <br />Like they reach a cliff and drop the last chapter <br />into unknown depths never to be finished. <br />They leave you emotionally reaching for something... <br />anything to fit the void...like chocolate or ice cream... <br />That's the cure for most literary voids right??? <br />But this book(series) builds to this great crescendo <br />and then slowly brings you back to earth, <br />gently planting your feet on solid ground, <br />then wrapping you in a gentle hug that leaves you smiling, <br />basking in its warm glow :) <br /><br />ok. <br />yeah? <br />cutesy. <br />Young. <br />but i did like it. <br />I have the first three books at this point if anyone wants them. <br />The last one u can get at the library or something <br />i think u will want to finish them! <br />good sleepy time books. <br /><br />Goodnight! <br />:) <br /><br />But now what will i read??? :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="6220755829385508288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1639779703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639779703" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16188188-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600525663p2/16188188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639779703?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/16188188-kerry">Kerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639779703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17835400333214894441">A thrilling and wonderful conclusion to this series. Maerad and Hem must find their way back to one another. As always though this is no easy feat and they must face danger, darkness and fight to save themselves and those they love. As always the adventures keep you gripped throughout and draw you into the magical world created within the pages of these books. <br/>A fabulous series I highly recommended it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1148163939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1148163939" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1849556-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528146595p2/1849556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1148163939?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/1849556-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763636654" href="/book/show/2833308-the-singing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1849556-maggie?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1148163939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4719866743045975100"><b>Did I enjoy it?</b> Yes, I thought this was the strongest book in the series. After lots of character and world building, we finally got to some actual plot.<br/><b>Would I read it again?</b> Possibly. I really don't know.<br/><b>Who would I recommend it to?</b> Fantasy fans, if you like Tamora Pierce, Mercedes Lackey, Tolkein, or other authors along those lines you'll probably like this, it's got a somewhat similar feel to it.<br/><b>Any other thoughts?</b> This book picks up where <i>The Crow</i> left off, but we're with Maerad again. The </span>
  <span id="freeText4719866743045975100" style="display:none"><b>Did I enjoy it?</b> Yes, I thought this was the strongest book in the series. After lots of character and world building, we finally got to some actual plot.<br /><b>Would I read it again?</b> Possibly. I really don't know.<br /><b>Who would I recommend it to?</b> Fantasy fans, if you like Tamora Pierce, Mercedes Lackey, Tolkein, or other authors along those lines you'll probably like this, it's got a somewhat similar feel to it.<br /><b>Any other thoughts?</b> This book picks up where <i>The Crow</i> left off, but we're with Maerad again. The chapters flip between Maerad and Hem until they finally reunite just over halfway through. I did think there was a pretty quick jump from the book's climax to the epilogue. I mean, I definitely didn't want another 100 pages describing them traveling back to Innail, but the action itself happened so quickly it took me a minute to figure out what had actually happened, and it was almost anti-climactic! For being told over and over again over the course of the four books that The Nameless One was the bad guy, I sure knew next to nothing about him by the time Maerad and Hem sang the Treesong and he was defeated. Additionally, I felt throughout the whole series that the relationships between all of the characters weren't very well explored/described. It felt obvious that Maerad and Cadvan would get together eventually, but their relationship never really feels like more than that of teacher and student. And Saliman's random love interest in this one felt like she came out of nowhere, and the plot could have continued without her just as well as with her. Really the most fully explored/explained relationships in the series were between Saliman and Hem, and Hem and Irk. I don't know why, but they were the most believable. Overall this series was mostly harmless, and a decent YA fantasy series that hits all of the usual tropes but in an engaging way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4719866743045975100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V/e1/rQTA+6XZjrbjdAsN2LhbY/wHinxk7wmEuXjR5hkBFp3p6vMfjg9oPsoDkJO7X7vGhCe6ygw40JKmT639A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fkZ2btQKw3j1WKn3z91970KPpElVpXfsSIX6CYwPJ0hNtZnnx7IM6FoDM9dqAxOWzRAm3LUltTXr2p5R8NLXJA==')})
  }
//]]>

Starting with her demolition of the Biblical myth that woman was an afterthought to the creation of man, Elaine Morgan rewrites human history and evolution.\nThis lively, informative book sets out to solve the riddle of our origins; its answer is controversial. Elaine Morgan has made The Aquatic Ape Hypothesis a plausible alternative to conventional theories of evolution and The Descent of Woman first set out an understanding of who humans are and where they came from.\nElaine Morgan was best known as a writer for television until the publication of The Descent of Woman in 1972, which became an international bestseller. She then spent ten years researching human evolution before publishing The Aquatic Ape (published by Souvenir Press as a revised edition, The Aquatic Ape Hypothesis) in 1982. In the years since, The Aquatic Ape Hypothesis has gone on to win widespread support among scientists.\nIt is a measure of Elaine Morgan\'s enduring importance, provocative thought and international reputation that in January 2006, the first Chinese translation of The Aquatic Ape Hypothesis became a Number 1 bestseller in Taiwan.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6245966976077900405\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4538693781009333044">Alison Croggon is the award winning author of the acclaimed fantasy series The Books of Pellinor. You can sign up to her monthly newsletter and receive a free Pellinor story at <a href='http://www.alisoncroggon.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>alisoncroggon.com</a><br/><br/>Her most recent book is Fleshers, the first in a dazzling new SF series co-written with her husband, acclaimed playwright Daniel Keene. Her latest Pellinor book, The Bone Queen, was a 2016 Aurealis Awards B</span>
  <span id="freeText4538693781009333044" style="display:none">Alison Croggon is the award winning author of the acclaimed fantasy series The Books of Pellinor. You can sign up to her monthly newsletter and receive a free Pellinor story at <a href="http://www.alisoncroggon.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">alisoncroggon.com</a><br /><br />Her most recent book is Fleshers, the first in a dazzling new SF series co-written with her husband, acclaimed playwright Daniel Keene. Her latest Pellinor book, The Bone Queen, was a 2016 Aurealis Awards Best Young Adult Book finalist. Other fantasy titles include Black Spring (shortlisted for the Young People's Writing Award in the 2014 NSW Premier's Literary Awards) and The River and the Book, winner of the Wilderness Society's prize for Environmental Writing for Children.<br /><br />She is a prize-winning poet and theatre critic,, and has released seven collections of poems. As a critic she was named Geraldine Pascall Critic of the Year in 2009. She also writes opera libretti, and the opera she co-wrote with Iain Grandage was Vocal/Choral Work of the Year in the 2015 Art Music Awards. Her libretto for Mayakovsky, score by Michael Smetanin, was shortlisted in the Drama Prize for the 2015 Victorian Premier's Literary Awards. She lives in Melbourne..</span>
